Women's Special

The Similarities and Differences Between British and American Women 181

— Zhu Ying

England is known for its cleanliness, order, and gentlemanly manners. Naturally, these merits cannot but be attributed to women. British women's skill in managing the home is the best in Europe. In every family in England, even if they are not very wealthy, even if they do not have servants to handle the labor, they always keep the home clean and orderly. Every day, the husband goes out to work, and the wife stays at home to sweep, dust, wash away dirt, and manage meals. When the husband returns home from work, he can always see a cheerful and lively wife, accompanying him for meals. Although such a housewife who is good at managing the home is so busy during the day, she still maintains a noble demeanor when she goes out for walks, recreation, or attends banquets with her husband in the evening. Furthermore, British women are very fond of saving. Although the husband's income is not very abundant, they will certainly be diligent and thrifty in saving some money for reserves. Before marriage, there are plenty who are self-sufficient through their occupations, but after marriage, more than 90% are in the home, managing the household for their husbands.

Although America and England are sister countries, the lives of American women are completely different from those of British women. American women are especially fond of enjoying themselves. The most feared thing for general American women is managing the home. Those with ample financial resources entrust sweeping and washing to servants. Those who cannot afford to hire servants simply move into apartments, so that even food does not need to be prepared by themselves. Therefore, in every family in America, although considerable cleanliness and order are maintained, it is generally not due to the housewife's efforts. American women are most particular about socializing. Women's activity in the social arena is far greater than that of men, so husbands cannot force their wives to be docile in the home. Moreover, husbands cannot force their wives to go out and play together. Women's occupations are much more developed in America than in England. Unmarried women are engaged in occupations, needless to say. Even married women, in general, still work outside. American women do not pay much attention to saving money. Because they all attach great importance to occupations and neglect the home, they also consider raising children to be a very troublesome matter. Therefore, the issue of birth control is not generally sympathized with by housewives in England, but in America, it has a very strong force. Because general American women all consider childbirth to be a great enemy of their career and social life.

As for the similarities between British and American women, there are also some. They are equally patriotic to their country. They are equally sympathetic to society. They are equally progressive about women's suffrage. They equally embrace a lifelong attitude of research towards learning. And the love of sports is also a common characteristic of British and American women.

Do We Really Need a Family? 182

— Chen Xue Zhao

In 1934, the Soviet newspaper "Pravda," recognizing the importance of this everyday life issue, raised the question "Seeking the Soviet Family" to solicit opinions from young people. How should we reconcile our personal private lives with society? This is a serious open question. The answer from most Soviet youths was: We want a family, we want a family that harmonizes our personal lives with society.

That is also my meaning. To put it concisely, I will quote the words of the scientist Langevin in his "The Individual and Society": "The more we participate in mass undertakings, the happier our personal lives will be." These words could not be more correct.

Looking at it this way, the lives of ordinary modern Chinese people cannot really be considered happy. They do not like suitable and moldy entertainment, such as plays, etc. They prefer to read novels and poems, alone among the flowers and under the moon, in the corner of the room, reading carefully, savouring carefully. They like to smoke opium, like to get snacks to eat. If they are a bit more modern, they go to dance halls, watch movies, make some friends, such so-called "living room gentlemen and ladies," today talking about this friend's love affairs, tomorrow talking about that wife's love history, moving their tongues, arguing, today getting along with this person, tomorrow not getting along with that person. Although they try their best to make their private lives a bit more lively, but turning over and over in their small circle, they are still weak; they lament the emptiness and boredom of life, they want to pursue the glory of the past in history, and forget that they themselves are the people who create history. They do not do this thing instead. Like the format of their lives? It is too biased towards the individual, too far away from society, they are like closing their own doors, naturally not tasting reasonable happiness. Conversely speaking, reasonable happiness requires harmonizing the individual and society, continuously adding my individual to the actions of society; at the same time, having a strong interest in any legitimate thing, a great optimistic attitude.

Sweden's Divorce Arbitration System 183

— Bu Ren

No one can deny that as the women's rights movement rises, divorce procedures are gradually becoming easier, and divorce cases are gradually increasing. The opinions of commentators on the pros and cons of easy divorce are quite inconsistent. Some believe that divorce should be absolutely free, and some advocate that the restrictions on divorce should be as strict as possible. In fact, there are certainly many who obtain satisfactory happiness after divorce, but there are also not a few who hastily divorce due to a moment of passion and regret it. In short, in a country where women's economic status cannot be completely independent, it is impossible to seek a divorce system without any drawbacks and a divorce trial that is completely fair and impartial. Recently, many people have advocated that before divorce cases are litigated in court, a separate handling agency should be established to engage in review and persuasion, in order to reduce unfortunate events that can be salvaged, because once an incompatible couple meets in court, both sides do their best to attack, and the judge relies entirely on legal clauses, and things reach the point of no return. In Sweden, which is known for its advanced women's rights movement, the authorities have taken the lead in implementing this claim. This is Sweden's divorce arbitration system.

In Sweden, a person who requests a divorce, whether it is unilateral or with mutual consent, must apply to the Divorce Arbitration Committee. The arbitration committee consists of two members, two women and one man, appointed by the Judicial Permanent Bureau. After receiving the divorce application, the Arbitration Committee engages in investigation, inquiry, and persuasion. If it believes that it fully meets the legal conditions for divorce and both parties insist that they do not want to reconcile, the committee will order temporary separation. The separation is for a period of one year, and a formal divorce certificate will be issued after the expiration of the term. According to statistics, out of one hundred couples requesting a divorce, twenty-five or more couples have had their divorce idea broken due to the committee's efforts in mediation, and thirty or more couples have achieved reconciliation and repaired the old relationship during the temporary separation period. This is to say that due to the establishment of the divorce arbitration system, the number of divorce cases in Sweden that have become a fact has decreased by more than half.

Mrs. Branting is one of the three members of the Swedish Divorce Arbitration Committee. She is the daughter of Branting, who served as the Prime Minister of Sweden for three years, and the founder of the Swedish Legal Aid Association, practicing law in the capital and gaining a great reputation. In a recent speech in New York, Mrs. Branting said to people: "Women leaving the family is gradually increasing; I do not believe that they want to do this, it is really the economic laws that force them to take this path. I believe that men and women living together is a common ideal, but this ideal must be based on mutual love and understanding rather than on an economic basis."

Looking at these words, we can imagine what kind of woman Mrs. Branting is who cares about family happiness. Her being selected as a divorce arbitration committee member related to the happiness of families across the country is certainly not accidental.

Special Feature of This Newspaper

An Interview with Liu Wang Liming 184

— Huang Ji Ping

Mrs. Wang Liming, wife of Liu Zhanen, president of Shanghai University, is known to everyone as an outstanding talent in the women's community. She studied in the United States, is good at speaking, and has a voice in the times. After returning to China, she has been serving the women's community for fifteen years. She has always advocated that Chinese society needs new virtuous wives and good mothers, which is generally praised. Yesterday at dusk, I had a ten-minute conversation with her at the Chinese Women's Temperance Union, and I thought it was very valuable, and now I faithfully report it to the readers.

Recent Photo of Liu Wang Liming 185

"Mrs. Liu, what was the most memorable thing about her student days?" This was my first question.

She thought for a while and said happily: "There are many memorable things, I can't say them all at once. Let me give you an example first. In 1918, when I was studying at Northwestern University in the United States, the school held a speech contest, and there were representatives from all levels, and there were people from all countries, but only Chinese people did not participate. I was very angry and dared not belittle myself. Many Chinese female students advised me not to make a fool of myself, because two years ago a Chinese student had failed, and everyone thought it was too dishonorable. I resolutely wanted to vent my anger and finally got third place. The following year, another contest was held, and I prepared early. As a result, I was lucky enough to get first place, so our classmates thought it was a great honor. In the same year, the Women's Christian Temperance Union held a summer conference at Late Geneva. In the evening, female representatives from various countries gave speeches. According to custom, there was no applause. I represented East Asia and also gave a long speech. As soon as I stepped down from the stage, the whole audience burst into applause and raised me high and scrambled to kiss me. Finally, I was able to raise my eyebrows for Chinese women, and the compatriots who were present felt very happy. These few things are not bragging, but to show that a woman should not give way when she should. When something happens, she must have the courage to take into account the dignity of the country everywhere. If she is timid and afraid, she will accomplish nothing."

"Mrs. Liu, how is her life as a housewife?"

"After I returned to China in 1920, I served at the Chinese Women's Temperance Union. In 1926, the union was reorganized and I was elected as the general secretary, and I have been doing so ever since. The year I got married was 1922. Originally, I worked full-time at the union. Because I was busy with housework after giving birth, I changed to handling household affairs in the morning and going to the union to work in the afternoon. I think being a mother is the greatest, most difficult, and most difficult job, which is different from doing other things. For example, child rearing, hygiene, management, nursing, etc., mothers must be able to speak and do. Not only that, but also family finances, cooking, sewing, assisting her husband's career, everything belongs to the scope of household affairs, which is much more difficult than teaching one or two subjects, or any other occupation. Therefore, I advocate new virtuous wives and good mothers, and they cannot give up their family responsibilities. Even if they have extra strength to serve society, they must reallocate their time after production. If they entrust household affairs to maids, that is a great loss. My ideal is that after the reform of the social system in the future, we will break the maid system, manage our own families, raise our own children; and even take care of our own food and clothing. This is reasonable."

Photograph of Parents and Children 186

"How does Mrs. Liu usually entertain herself?"

"I don't have much entertainment. I just play with my children in my leisure time. I have two sons and one daughter, which is enough to keep me busy. They play ball when they want to play ball, and play games when they want to play games: this is what I like the most. Sometimes I plant flowers with them and appreciate the beautiful flowers and plants. Every night, I supervise them to study for two hours. Sometimes, I engage in writing. These are all my ways of entertaining myself."

"What criticism does Mrs. Liu have of urban women?"

"I don't want to criticize, but they have two common problems: Most women will get married, but they are completely unprepared before marriage, such as in terms of household education. Most of them know nothing. After marriage, they are not united at all. Most women are enthusiastic about public affairs when they are in school, but after marriage, they suddenly change their attitude and never care about social welfare undertakings. In social banquets, they are gorgeously dressed, like flowers and jade, actively participating. When they have free time, they play cards and watch movies for fun. They don't read books or newspapers all day long, and they don't care about their children. Children born in such families are not happy, but simply suffering! It is not as good as the family happiness of poor mothers and children embracing each other all the time. These can be said to be the degeneration of life and the degeneration of the spirit. I often say that if a woman cannot make her family management scientific, her life rational, her furnishings artistic, and her economy thrifty after marriage, and at the same time does not have a proper understanding of society, does not fulfill her civic obligations, and does not take on the responsibility of saving the country, then she cannot be considered a wife and mother of the times."

"So, which way does Mrs. Liu think modern women should go?" This was my question before and after. "It would take a long time to explain this. In short, in addition to managing the family, modern women should have a sound personality, seek the evolution of society, and fulfill their national duties. The work that should be done at present, such as abolishing concubines, prohibiting prostitution, rescuing female beggars, prohibiting keeping maids, and helping unemployed women...etc., are all matters of women themselves and should be united to relieve the suffering of the public. In short, saving the country and the people is not only the responsibility of men. To revive the nation, women need to promote it. That is all I want to say at the moment!"

Short Story

A Ray of Hope 187

— Hao Wu

The baby's unease and crying intensified day by day! Especially on that windy and rainy night, the crying sound changed from loud to hoarse, intermittent. When the family members changed the swaddling clothes for the baby, they suddenly discovered that the cloth strip wrapping the umbilical cord had come off its original position; the severed end of the umbilical cord protruded moistly outside the navel.

Consequently, the mother's milk could not be smoothly sucked into the baby's mouth due to spasms in the baby's mouth.

The family members were bewildered. The old and frail midwife then came to fumigate the baby's ears for a while and determined that this was an "incurable lockjaw fright." However, the sorceress who communicated with ghosts and gods (?) confidently said after a series of actions: "The disease will turn for the better - and in the near future."

A reassurance pill rolled into the family's esophagus: "Then we don't have to panic!"

The baby lived, struggling! Bluish-purple skin, thin and bony face; refused to eat, whimpering and crying, cry! Work hard, little life; because it's just there! Because only in your weak cry is there still a ray of hope.

Go to the Kitchen - Family Recipes 188

— Gu Liyun

"Three days after marriage, she enters the kitchen and washes her hands to make soup;" wives and daughters must study cooking. In these recessionary years, you must not make jokes about eating a free meal when managing the household. "Returning to the kitchen" is not a shameful thing. Especially in this era of rich world but poor people, we should bury our heads and work hard. Do everything yourself and cook your own meals!

Cooking; The control of ingredients is certainly a major issue, as the saying goes: "Even a clever woman cannot cook without rice," but the sweetness and saltiness of the seasoning, the intensity of the heat, and cooking all have important relationships; A good cook can make even vegetables and tofu delicious, otherwise, even the most precious delicacies will taste like chewing wax, so the heat and seasoning of dishes are very important in cooking.

Now, I will list a few dishes with different cooking methods:

Hundred Treasure Wild Duck Wild duck is a special product of Taihu Lake. In Suzhou, live ones are sold in the market in winter. There are also several wild game shops that sell cooked wild duck, only doing business in winter and spring. However, that kind of cooked wild duck is only suitable for wine and porridge. It is better to cook rice dishes yourself. Stewed wild duck is not as tasty as braised. After gutting the wild duck, stuff it with glutinous rice mixed with minced pork or chestnuts, etc., and then braise it with seasonings. Put it in a casserole and simmer it on a charcoal stove. It is fragrant, fatty, and delicious.

Winter Bamboo Shoots with Shredded Meat First, pick and wash the shepherd's purse, then cut the meat and winter bamboo shoots into thin shreds, then heat oil and stir-fry them. For all stir-fried dishes in cooking, such as stir-fried shrimp, stir-fried shredded meat, etc., the oil must be hot, and the fire must be strong. After heating it very strongly, put in the shrimp, etc., and stir-fry it slightly with a spatula. The shrimp, etc., that are cooked are both cooked and tender, and very fresh. If the oil is not hot enough, the dishes will not be fresh and tender, and the taste will be very different. Of course, stir-fried shepherd's purse with shredded meat and winter bamboo shoots is also cooked in the same way. After putting the shredded meat into the pot, put in the shepherd's purse and winter bamboo shoots immediately. Cook it over high heat, slightly piercing through, then serve it up. The taste is very delicious.

Shrimp Balls and Fish Balls When serving hot pot, shrimp balls and fish balls are also essential dishes in the family. The cooking method of shrimp balls is to first mash two scallion whites together with the shrimp meat, then add two or three egg yolks depending on the amount of shrimp meat, mash and mix them, then add some rice wine and mix well; then boil a pot of boiling water and make the shrimp meat paste into balls one by one and throw them into the water. When the shrimp balls are thrown into the water, the fire at the bottom of the pot only needs to maintain the temperature of the water, burning as if there is no fire, then the cooked shrimp balls will be tender and fresh. If the heat is too strong, then the shrimp balls will be old and tasteless. The method of making fish balls is roughly the same as that of shrimp balls, but the procedure of scraping the fish fillets and removing the fine bones is a bit troublesome, and the eggs mixed into the fish paste must use egg whites. After the fish balls are made, they are like crystal balls.

Special Announcement from this Publication We are very grateful to the women's community and readers for their many contributions since the publication of this magazine. However, after calculating the number of words, nineteen articles are around 1,000 words, which makes publication very difficult. From now on, each article is limited to 600 words. We hope you will understand.

Sincerely, Editorial Department.

Drifting (Part 2) 189

— Qin Wang Yin Jiu

In the week after school, Qiu Yun was really busy enough, preparing everything needed to go to America, wishing she could complete everything in one breath, even to the point of not being able to sleep for several nights. Suddenly one day, her cousin came; the cousin was a young mother who was already married and had a two-year-old son. She had the best relationship with Qiu Yun on weekdays. Her husband worked as a traveling accountant in a large company and often went out. Whenever he went out, the cousin would invite her to live with her. This time he went to Fujian again, and the cousin came to invite her again. She really didn't want to go, but her mother saw that she was too tired from being busy and hoped that she could rest for a while, so she tried her best to persuade her, and Qiu Yun finally agreed.

Although she was very lively and generous, she had never been close to men. When her brother's friends came to her house, she would only give a few brief greetings and was too lazy to talk. When one-sided love letters were thrown in, she would always tear them up as soon as she opened them. This time, after she went to her cousin's house, she found that her cousin had recently developed a hobby, which was playing cards. The reason was very simple, because a gambling family had recently moved in next door, and the sound of cards could be heard every day. However, there were no outsiders in the gambling, only a few family members. So, the cousin pulled them along. When Qiu Yun went, the cousin naturally wanted to try her best to win her over, and also explained that there were no men in this family except for two old men. Qiu Yun couldn't refuse firmly, so she went and played a few rounds of cards. Unexpectedly, one day, a young man with very gorgeous clothes and a very gentle manner suddenly came to the card table. At first, he said he was replacing the old lady, but later he replaced her for a long time. At that time, Qiu Yun was losing very badly, and this gentleman happened to be sitting to her left, so he tried his best to help her. Every time he played a card, it was beneficial to Qiu Yun; this had already made Qiu Yun very happy, and the man's words were particularly seductive. Every time he said a word, he could always make people sympathize. By the end of the game, his shadow had been deeply embedded in Qiu Yun's mind. From then on, this man came to play cards with Qiu Yun every day, and the power of temptation increased day by day, to the point where Qiu Yun's intelligence was completely confused, and the preparations for studying abroad completely stopped. Her father's urging created an opportunity for the man to encourage Qiu Yun to elope:

Two or three years later, that man appeared in the local area again and officially married another woman, while the poor Qiu Yun did not know where she had drifted to, breaking away from this world with her happiness.

Standard Woman

Mrs. Kalinin 190

— Shen Yu

Mrs. Kalinin, Ivanovna, has become a female hero of the contemporary Soviet Union. Her deeds can be compared to her husband Kalinin (Chairman of the People's Committee of the Soviet Union), because although she is the chairman's wife, she is determined to be an independent woman. She devoted her life's energy to the reclamation of the barren land in the mountains of Siberia.

Originally, four years ago, she left the bustling Moscow and, with a spirit of fearlessness, established a large farm and a cultural center among the nomadic Altai people.

She is busy with construction work all day long, digging ponds, building power plants, raising bees and other livestock, and training students. In short, although she is already in her 50s, she lives a simple life and puts all her energy into the construction of Altai. Therefore, a large farm that supplies food to the entire region, a national school that instills culture, and children who can read and write have now been established there.

The Altai people used to use flint to make fire, but now they also have new-style electric lights.

Therefore, no matter how barren a place is, as long as someone can sacrifice everything to work hard to reclaim it, it can be made prosperous. Isn't Mrs. Kalinin's success a very obvious example?

Women like Mrs. Kalinin are worthy of praise and can be said to be female heroes standing at the forefront of the times!

Shenbao Local Supplement

Talks

Welcoming Mr. Hu Hanmin 191

— Fang Ke

Mr. Hu Hanmin has returned from overseas and is now about to arrive in Hong Kong. It is said that soon, he will make a special trip north to take office as the chairman of the Central Standing Committee. The central government has specially appointed welcoming officials Ye Chucang, Ju Zheng, Chen Ce, and other gentlemen to go south. The "Shanghai All-Circles Preparatory Committee for Welcoming Chairman Hu Zhantang to Beijing for Office" organized by various circles in Shanghai has also been established, all of which are sufficient to be the "overture" to this grand event.

The Shanghai Welcoming Hu Preparatory Committee once had a proposal: to send letters to various newspapers requesting them to write articles to welcome Mr. Hu on the day of his arrival in Shanghai. Now, although Mr. Hu Hanmin has not yet arrived in Shanghai, publishing this article seems to be a bit premature, but welcoming him early can also show the sincerity of our expectations and the eagerness of our welcome.

Mr. Hu's return to China coincides with a time when people's livelihood is declining and the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent. Internally, people's livelihood is haggard and disaster victims are everywhere. Externally, the depth of the national crisis has changed from the Hebei-Chahar issue to the Suiyuan-East issue and even the Shandong issue. Moreover, the patriotic student movement is encountering obstacles everywhere. At this time, hearing the news that Mr. Hu Hanmin has returned to China to preside over the central government, we are truly overjoyed and cannot express it in words.

Mr. Hu's support and welcome can be seen not only from the central government's special appointment of officials to welcome him south and the establishment of welcome committees in various places, but also from the earnest expectations and sincerity of those engaged in patriotic movements in various places for Mr. Hu, which must be ten or a hundred times greater than the current manifestation of facts. They earnestly expect that the day Mr. Hu takes office will be the day when the national fortune of the Republic of China will be reversed, the day when the patriotic movement will receive effective protection, the day when revolutionary diplomacy will be implemented, and the day when the various demands put forward by those engaged in this patriotic movement will be implemented.

The patriotic movement should be effectively protected, there should be absolute freedom of speech, publication, assembly, and association, and revolutionary diplomacy should be vigorously implemented. These, these are all contained in the platform of the Chinese Kuomintang, which is also what Mr. Hu Hanmin has always strongly advocated. In the past, because Mr. Hu was far away in a different place and relinquished power, his advocacy could not be fully implemented. This time, he has the honor to serve as the chairman of the Central Standing Committee and preside over the central government. These minimum demands of the people, which are also what Mr. Hu usually advocates, are hoped to be realized starting from the day he takes office!

Of course, our desired minimum requirements are not to ask for a piece of paper, that is, to complete things, and we dare to request to practice them after a piece of paper is announced. In other words, what we require is not a paper check, but a full realization.

In addition, how to relieve the national industry and commerce? How to urgently relieve the disaster-stricken people and prevent disasters? These are all eagerly hoped by the people who are in dire straits. However, although these two items are equally important, they may not be effective immediately on the day of taking office. It is better to protect the patriotic movement and lift the ban on freedom of speech, publication, assembly, and association, which are easier to achieve.

Mr. Hu is a revolutionary leader and a mentor to young people. He will surely express his acceptance of these minimum demands of the people and these minimum demands of national self-salvation with the utmost sincerity, and there is no doubt about it. The reason why we are tirelessly speaking is to ask Mr. Hu to express his determination to earnestly implement the various articles requested by the people on the day he takes office to comfort the people's expectations.

Now that the national crisis is becoming increasingly urgent, the people have no time and cannot accept any more "checks".

What we want is ironclad facts!

Golden Hair Waving Oars 192

— Xia Tianwu

I lived in Beihongsha for a period of time, and I had to go to Grandpa Duo's bean and wheat shop every day to record the account book: from my residence to the bean and wheat shop, there was a Huansha River in between, so I had to do the business of Golden Hair Waving Oars twice a day.

The first time I met Golden Hair Waving Oars was in early summer, because I was new to Beihongsha and unfamiliar with the route. Uncle Shun Sheng took me aboard Golden Hair Waving Oars' ferry. Uncle Shun Sheng patted Golden Hair's back and pointed at me, saying: "This is the newly arrived Mr. Jiang from Grandpa Duo's shop. From now on, he will make you two meals of water tobacco money every day!"

Oar-waving Golden Hair was in his fifties. After hearing Uncle Shun Sheng's words, he dragged out two deep-wrinkled smiles at the edge of his sparse white beard. His face looked very dry, and his back was a little curved. Sometimes, he would cough hoarsely once or twice. This situation really showed his old age, but what made people disbelieve was that his hands could row the oars so nimbly. The nickname "Oar-waving Golden Hair" was probably given to him for this reason.

"You've been eating this rowing rice for a long time, haven't you?" I asked.

"Hehe! A long time! A long time! This oar was passed down from my old man's hands, and I've been doing this since I was a child."

"Is your livelihood based on this?"

"Our three generations have been eating on this riverbank. The Yang family brushes cloth and the Jin family ferries. Our Jin family even erected a sticker at this ferry during the former Qing Dynasty!"

"That's a pretty good income!"

"Not bad. In my old man's hands, one copper coin was worth one yellow ticket. A round trip could earn four cash. Relying on this oar, I also passed down a five-room hall to my father. Now that we're talking about copper cents, if we make twenty or thirty round trips a day, we can earn three or four thousand cash. The family can get by."

As he spoke, the smiles dragged out again at the edge of his sparse white beard. These smiles contained his satisfaction with life. The ferry arrived. He put up his oars, we went ashore, and as he rowed back, I heard him sing a mountain song: "The first silkworm doesn't look at the second silkworm, the wheat isn't harvested until the dragon boat is rowed..."

Because I passed through this ferry every day, the smiles at the edge of Oar-waving Golden Hair's white beard and the sound of his hoarse throat left a cordial impression on my brain until I left Beihongsha, and I could still easily think of him.

A few days after the Dragon Boat Festival last year, because Grandpa Duo died, I had to go to Beihongsha again. When I passed through the ferry, Oar-waving Golden Hair was still there, but what made me very strange was that his demeanor was different from before. He showed a sense of decadence amidst his old age. He hadn't seen me for a long time, so at least a few smiles should have unfolded at the edge of his white beard, but there was no joy on his face at all. I couldn't help but ask casually: "Golden Hair, are there any prizes for the dragon boats in Hongsha this year?"

"Who has the heart to make a fuss about the dragon boats? The days to come will be a matter of seeing there is no food to eat."

"What's the matter?"

"Mr. Jiang, don't you know? Poor people's mouths can't cause trouble. I blinded myself and ended up cutting off my own livelihood. A few days ago, the father-in-law of Grandpa Yang from the east came to Hongsha and also ferried across this Huansha River. As soon as he got on the boat, he kept urging me to row faster and faster, wishing he could step onto the ferry in one step. I didn't recognize him. When he urged me, I opened my mouth and said: "Old sir, with one oar, I can only row at a speed of first-class and second-class water. If you want to go faster, the water can't be like a good road on land. You just wait for the bridge to be built and you can take big steps across it." I didn't expect that the last sentence offended him. This father-in-law of Grandpa Yang went back and talked to Grandpa Yang, and they agreed to build a stone bridge there in Xihongtou. Don't you think that in this way, my livelihood will be cut off?"

As he spoke, he pointed to Xihongtou for me to see. I looked in the direction of his finger and indeed saw a few long and wide bridge deck stones piled up on the fields of Xihongtou. I said: "Why didn't you go to Grandpa Yang later to plead for mercy?"

"Alas! Mr. Jiang, how could I not think of it? As soon as I got the news, the whole family went to beg Grandpa Yang, but Grandpa Yang said: "It's useless for you to ask me. My father-in-law has never been someone who can be pushed around. What's more, it's you? Now that he's already made up his mind about this matter, and the township office also agrees with him!"... Mr. Jiang, I'm already at this old age, but I didn't expect to suffer this misfortune. This old bone can only row a slow and intermittent oar. What else can I do to make a living? Isn't the whole family's livelihood ruined?"

His voice echoed in my ears, making me unable to muster the courage to answer him. I didn't even dare to look at his face before stepping onto the dike and leaving.

After taking care of Grandpa Duo's funeral, the new stone bridge in Xihongtou had been completed. I stood at that ferry and looked around, but I couldn't see the shadow of Oar-waving Golden Hair and his old ferry. I could only walk onto the new stone bridge. As I walked in the middle of the bridge, looking at the middle of the Huansha River, it seemed as if Oar-waving Golden Hair was on the ferry, looking at me with tears of despair and resentment in his eyes, unblinking.

Page 18

A Peculiar Person 193

— Ye Lai

At daybreak, the faint sounds and vibrations from the engine room of the steamer roused me in Humen. By this time, the ticket collectors, a tall man with a long face and a stout man with a protruding chest, had appeared solemnly in our fourth-class cabin. I silently watched their two alert and sharp eyes scan the faces of the thirty or forty passengers. When a typical northerner with a sallow face looked at them timidly, they shouted:

"Tickets!" But when the passenger was too afraid to speak, they slapped him a few times, saying, "You rogue, don't you have money to take the ship? Get off at Shantou!"

After being slapped a few times, the passenger, with reddened eyes, fled away with his only possession, a blue serge shirt. The ticket collectors then yelled and cursed at other similar people.

But what was strange was a passenger next to me. From his conversation with his companions, one could tell he was from Meixian. He had been wandering since childhood, spent many years in Guangxi, worked as a soldier and as a minor clerk. He looked to be about twenty-four or twenty-five years old. His triangular eyes, filled with anger and ferocity, were paired with high, sharp cheekbones, a thin and very swarthy face, and unclean teeth peeking out from his thin lips. He was constantly grinding his teeth, as if to show he had endured endless misery and was surrounded by nothing but hateful things. However, he pretended to be a knowledgeable person with a lot of experience. In his worn wicker basket was a set of Western clothes, and he was wearing a very new rayon shirt. No one would have believed he couldn't afford an eight-dollar ticket. But this time, he really puffed out his chest and said he had no money. The two ticket collectors glared at him, their eyes wide:

"What? You have no money? Who believes that? Take it out now, or you'll be thrown off!"

"I'm going to Shanghai. If I didn't buy a ticket, I wouldn't be here. This ship belongs to the government, why can't we ride it?" He also roared angrily, staring at them with his triangular eyes: "No money!"

"You say you have no money? We'll search you. The shipping company belongs to the country, but the business is run by compradores. You have no conscience! Hmph! You bastard! Rogue!"

He was so choked by their cursing that his face turned red, and he secretly pulled out two dollars from his pocket, but then looked at them fearfully and said:

"I only have this much money. Do you want it?"

The ticket collector glared at him resentfully and quickly snatched his money:

"Not even enough to buy a ticket. We'll let you off this time, but you have to get off at Shantou. Shameless fellow!"

"No! I gave you money to buy a ticket. I want to go to Shanghai, not Shantou!"

He cried anxiously, but the ticket collectors had already left. All the passengers were looking at him strangely. At this time, his face turned even redder, and he seemed to smile sadly, saying:

"This ship belongs to the country. It's for the people. Why should I spend money? I have money, I'm not that stupid. When I get to Shanghai, I'll take the train to Nanjing, but I won't buy a ticket!"

He said victoriously, then looked at a Guangxi man next to him and grinned.

The ship sailed for a day and a night, arriving in Shantou. Those who hadn't bought tickets quietly left the ship. But the man who hadn't bought enough of a ticket put on his ill-fitting autumn suit, as if he hadn't suffered any humiliation. He cheerfully ran back and forth on the deck and even went ashore to play. At noon, the sunlight gently touched the pale green water of the sea, touched the open-air fourth-class cabin, and was quiet. Not many passengers remained here. I began to silently watch the singing girls wandering on the ship and their faces with bitter smiles.

The passenger returned, bringing fresh fruit produced in Shantou, and he and several Guangxi people were eating and talking.

A fourteen-year-old singing girl smiled and agreed to their request, singing those unpleasant "Eighteen Touches" songs. He nestled close to her, listening with his triangular eyes glazed over. One song after another was sung. When she pleaded with them for money, he slowly shook his head, as if dissatisfied with the singing, and smiled bitterly, taking out two jiao coins.

"Not enough, sir! And these jiao coins are hard to use!" She looked at him coquettishly, twisting and turning. "Please help me. My family of eight relies on this to survive!"

"What? Who wants to listen to your bad songs? Get lost! Get lost! Damn you!"

The passenger roared angrily, his face fierce, grinding his teeth, as if driving something away. The singing girl was startled by his shout and walked away in tears. Then, he looked at his companions victoriously and laughed heartily, as if thinking his soul was so noble.

"This world! I've suffered a lot, but I also want to show my authority! It has to be this way!"

His joyful appearance and his words stunned me. I looked at this peculiar person in pain and remained silent.

Welcoming the God of Joy 194

— Li Xuan

Small firecrackers crackled like popping beans under the eaves of every house, and the night slowly revealed its ashen grayness.

The shady parts of the house were still dark. The wick in the oil lamp emitted a small flame, flickering with a faint, dim light. Dad rubbed his red, sleepless eyes with his sleeve, coughed twice against the wall, took a breath, tapped the ashes from his pipe onto the windowsill, and said to Mom:

"Go make dumplings. People are already setting off firecrackers at dawn."

Mom quietly stepped out the door and brought some sorghum stalks from the yard. She added water to the pot in the outer room, and the sorghum stalks crackled in the stove like damp firecrackers. Dad remained blankly in a daze. He hadn't been back for long. He had left on the day of the kitchen god festival. High-legged Li from the Shuangshengxing Pharmacy had looked for him several times, and the Hongchang family came every day. Mom cried to them and swore that Dad had joined the army. But they didn't believe it. High-legged Li said as he left:

"He's hiding. He can hide until he's thirty this year, but not past the first day of next year."

Everyone else was offering sacrifices and eating dumplings. Dad ran back covered in a thick layer of snow. Mom twisted him around, brushed the snow off his clothes, and he climbed onto the kang and started smoking. After a while, he sniffled and sighed with a worried frown.

At this moment, Mom put the dumplings into the pot one by one and stirred them with a spoon. The wick burning in the lamp crackled, the flame flickered, and the lamp went out with a "squeak." The room was suddenly filled with darkness. The large, chessboard-like window cast a square of pale light.

"Go welcome the God of Joy. Little Baozi, go with your dad."

Dad grunted when he heard Mom's words. He put his pipe on the windowsill, climbed down from the kang, and said while putting on his "monkey-cap":

"Welcoming the God of Joy, he won't come to our house anyway. He only goes to the homes of the fortunate."

"Don't talk about unlucky things on the fifth watch of the New Year."

Mom grumbled as she came into the room, put the big red cotton hat on me, tied the leg straps, and took me off the ground, instructing:

"Kowtow sincerely, hoping we'll have a better year!"

Dad took the God of Joy print from the Kitchen God table, took out three long incense sticks, and led me out of the house. The snow had stopped, and the wind howled sharply, making my face feel sore and painful. I didn't want Dad to hold my hand and rubbed my face with my hands. After a while, my hands felt swollen and numb. Dad looked at me, smiled, and carried me in his left arm. Going down the riverbank was scary. The planks were covered with ice. Dad's feet slipped accidentally, and we slowly walked down the slope step by step. There was a large expanse of white snow on the river beach. The river was covered with thick ice. The snow, like a furry, shimmering blanket, lay quietly across to the endless fields on the opposite bank. The green wheat seedlings were buried under the glittering snow layer. The entire gray sky was covered with a shimmering white light, and the cold wind swirled with fine ice particles.

The small food stall by the bridge was closed, cold and empty. Two dogs were chasing each other in front of the door. A tall merchant walked over from the bridge, with a ledger on his shoulder and a "dalian" for holding money.

"Tch, that debt collector, coming back at dawn."

Dad said, putting me down and pointing it out to me. After he finished speaking, he lit the incense and stuck it into the thick snow. He burned the God of Joy print. Dad knelt down, kowtowing towards the north, and said:

"God of Joy, bless me with a smooth year, and I'll give you a new robe and gild you."

After he finished kowtowing, he brushed the snow off his legs. I also ran down. The merchant staggered over. I had just kowtowed once.

"Your family said you joined the army. Well, don't you think, if Shuangshengxing hadn't lent you medicine, you say, at this time..."

"Hey, Shopkeeper Li, I won't forget your kindness. I'll definitely pay you back when I find a long-term job this year."

"It's the first day of the New Year tomorrow. In principle, I shouldn't be asking for debts anymore, but I still have debt collectors from Jizhou Pharmacy lying in my house. Give me a bit of it by the tenth of the month..."

Dad hesitated and agreed, picked me up, and ran home in a panic. As soon as he entered the door, he sighed loudly and said:

"God of Joy! As soon as I go out, it's a god of misfortune!"

Note: "Hiding" means avoiding creditors before the New Year. "God of Joy print" means a woodblock-printed image of the God of Joy.

Broadcast Schedule

Special Programs 195

Nine-Nine Art Society Broadcast Drama Group, East China (1360), 10:00 AM to 11:30 AM. Performers: Fang Rong, Lü Wei, Yong Hai, Yang Bang, Yang Kun.

Old Man Liu

Old Man Liu is a renowned hero in the martial arts world, known for his chivalry. His good friend, Zheng Ermazi, a platoon leader in the army, killed his superior—the battalion commander—out of righteous indignation for his heinous deeds. Although the battalion commander was wicked, military law could not be evaded. Zheng Ermazi was wounded and fled to Old Man Liu's doorstep. However, Old Man Liu was away on a mission with bandits, and only his son, Guangzu, was home. Zheng Ermazi begged Guangzu to let him hide, but Guangzu was a cunning young man who hated Zheng Ermazi for often speaking ill of him to his father. Therefore, he refused to take him in. Meanwhile, Platoon Leader Wang, leading soldiers, was quickly approaching in pursuit of Zheng Ermazi.

In this desperate situation, Zheng Ermazi finally secured refuge at the cost of two dollars. Platoon Leader Wang arrived at this time, and unable to find Zheng Ermazi, he tempted Guangzu with a gold watch. A gold watch ultimately outweighed two dollars, and Zheng Ermazi was betrayed.

Old Man Liu returned and saw that his friend had been harmed by his son. Furthermore, Zheng Ermazi cursed him as a "treacherous friend," tarnishing Old Man Liu's lifelong reputation. In the end, what happened to Zheng Ermazi? He was captured. What happened to the gold watch? It was smashed. And what happened to his son? He was shot!

Storytelling 197

Cheng Fangzhou, Li Liansun, Mao Jiashu

Huamei (1060), 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening "Human Qixi Festival"

Ten thousand zhang of the Milky Way hang in the blue sky. The light flows swiftly, and the autumn wind returns. The Weaver Girl and Cowherd meet once a year. How much longing in a single evening. I know, the Emperor's son is called Weaver Girl. Lonely in her boudoir in the east of the river. Year after year, she weaves diligently. The seamless heavenly robe is a peerless masterpiece. Therefore, the Emperor took pity on her living alone. He permitted her to marry a young cowherd west of the river. Who knew that once their hearts were joined, they became lazy. The Emperor ordered her to return and live east of the river. From then on, they could not visit often. They could only meet once a year. The matter is vague, but the sentiment is believable. Know that without diligence and thrift, there is no success. The same principle applies to heaven and earth. Diligence and thrift are endlessly useful. I know, the Cowherd was a poor man. How could he become a son-in-law in the heavenly palace. Wealth and poverty should be different and hard to match. Marriages in the world are also the same. Therefore, do not envy the wife's wealth and pursue it. Do not be greedy for gifts and turn your eyes red. Marital union does not depend on gold and jewels. Like-mindedness and mutual affection are essential. A scholarly couple studies together. Husband and wife follow each other in harmony and joy. It is also said that on the day the Cowherd married the Heavenly Granddaughter. He owed a bride price of ten thousand pairs of gold. Therefore, he was punished to herd cattle hard for a lifetime. Punished to meet only once a year. If the bride price is not paid off. It will be difficult to dream together in the same bed. Anecdotes and strange events are commonly told. All are in a vague place. However, I have other feelings to embellish. I remotely present a green message to the heavenly palace. I beg the Emperor to grant a great wish. Do not let the Heavenly Granddaughter live east of the river. The bride price of ten thousand dollars should be completely waived to relieve poverty. Moreover, this year's weather is even more peculiar. Droughts and floods are heavy. I hope to use the bride price as relief funds. To spread rain and dew and bathe in benevolent winds. If the Emperor approves my request. I will certainly be terrified and grateful to the heavens. Water, drought, and war are everywhere. How can the heavens comply with everything. I am just writing my heart to ease my mind.

Xia Hesheng's Three Smiles Guo Ben (800), 7:00 PM to 8:00 PM

Opening "Thousand Year Blessing"

Living in the Ten Scenic Spots of West Lake. Half village, half city, a watery land. Plant weeping willows in front of the door. Bamboo leaves and banana trees peek through the pink walls. Parents are both healthy and vigorous in the hall. Osmanthus trees in the courtyard are fragrant. Red sleeves and red smiles are the maids. Peach Root and Peach Leaf are the concubines. Why must family wealth be as rich as Tao Zhu's. A thousand acres of fertile fields are a small fortune. Those who come and go are learned guests. Li Bai, Su Dongpo, Zhao Ziyang. Wang Youjun, Fenbu, Mi Xiangyang. They talk about the five relationships and family matters. Nothing more than songs and essays. Strolling leisurely in Jin Valley Garden. Reading the Romance of the West Chamber on a sandalwood couch. Fine wine and delicious food bring ease. Three feet of snow does not lack grain. Sometimes, a game of chess. Sometimes, a furnace of incense. Sometimes, listening to a book. Sometimes, playing mahjong. Sometimes, a clear song revolves around the painted beams. Life is blessed to this point. Three hundred thousand years and sixty thousand zhang. Why must politicians bother.

Du Wenkui, Zhou Jianhong, Big Red Robe

China and the West (1040), 12:15 AM to 1:00 AM

Opening "Busy Socializing"

Wind, flowers, snow, and moon are lively. Joyful celebrations and funerals cost a lot of money. Zhao, Qian, Sun, Li, Zhou, Wu, Zheng. It is hard to distinguish between the three strokes of Wang and the grass head Huang. Funeral notices and invitations are not to be mentioned. Sixteenth and seventieth birthdays are definitely celebrated. A one-cent stamp travels all over the world. Unobstructed in all directions. Friendships are everywhere. Spring breeze and summer rain are appropriate. However, people in the interior are already afraid of the pain of socializing. The taste of Shanghai is even harder to bear. Small children's full month or birthday. Sending out an invitation is no problem. The mistress of the house. Twenty or thirty years old. A grand banquet is held to celebrate the beautiful hall. The person in question is even more lively. Minor celebrations are held on ordinary days. Furthermore, every family honors ancestors. They are not willing to forget the birthdays of their ancestors. Filial sons and virtuous grandsons are praised by everyone. Red signatures and couplets are written on incense. If, in the darkness, they could know. They would smile happily in the Yellow Springs. Anniversaries are calculated separately. In addition, some people have ancestral halls. Turning around year after year. Red and white invitations are like urging for grain. Or it may be that the Zhang family misses, the Li family sends. Tomorrow there will be no discussion. It can be seen in society. The ways of the world have always been cold and warm. It does not matter whether they are rich merchants. Families with economies are secretly hurt. Especially, the poor who have a difficult life. They have to put on a facade and force themselves to appear. People do not consider everyone's strength. The gift-giver secretly shouts injustice. They issue invitations and invite guests on behalf of others. The only fear is that teachers will have to be let go one after another in the future. I say that we should transform social customs and respect practicality. Socializing does not have to be extravagant. Every family has weddings and funerals. Unnecessary socializing needs to be improved. Do not follow the superficial customs and learn vanity.

Movie News

"Moonlight and Flowers" Two Leads Co-Star in New Film, "Smoke Waves of Joy" Opens at the Great Light 199

Dick Powell and Rose Gyllen co-star in the new film "Shipmates Forever," which opened at the Great Light yesterday. The two stars' previous film, "Moonlight and Flowers," is still popular today. Their renewed collaboration is even more amazing. Dick Powell sings several famous songs in the film, which are now popular throughout the United States. Rose Gyllen performs the most valuable dance in the film, which is even more valuable. The dance shadows of the sea waves are interesting and reflect each other. The arrogant laughter is dyed into one piece. Every place can be fascinating. It is a rare work in song and dance films. The director is Bao Caiqi, who has been famous in the directing world since the release of "Seventh Heaven," and Warner's previous production of "Moonlight and Flowers" was also directed by him.

Upcoming Performance of "Wild Geese Descending on the Han River" 200

The performance of "Raindrops on Pear Blossoms" received extraordinary support from the audience and high praise from the public opinion world. This can be said to be a great comfort to the initial collaborative achievements of the playwright Ma Xuweibang and the leading actor Chen Yanyan. So they decided to continue to collaborate on this "Wild Geese Descending on the Han River," with the joint efforts of Diao Banhua, Luo Peng, and many others.

During the year-long production period, the workers have been racking their brains and concentrating their efforts. We can see that its achievements have clearly surpassed the previous work of "Raindrops on Pear Blossoms" and have a further success.

When Ma Xu was writing the script for "Wild Geese Descending on the Han River," he had already decided on the cast, so the script is not only suitable for Chen Yanyan's personality, but it can also be said to be more suitable for the personality of each performer.

In order to achieve satisfactory scenery, "Wild Geese Descending on the Han River" not only spent a lot of effort on the photography field of the interior scenes, but also took the exterior scenes from afar in Putuo, a scenic beauty, where they collected many beautiful pictures and backgrounds by extracting the essence.

Here, focusing on the subject matter itself, in addition to clarifying its social significance, it also created a very strong tragic atmosphere, and the beautiful and sad scene in the first half is enough to make the audience's hearts turn.

Chen Yanyan filmed the scene of falling into the water in the cold winter weather, Diao Banhua had more amazing achievements than in "Autumn Fan Bright Lamp", and Luo Peng took on the very heavy role of the male lead. Ma Xuweibang made use of his superb makeup skills to play a strange old man.

This film will be released soon.

"Private Tide" Opens in Paris 201

The film "Raging Tide," which opened today at the Paris Grand Theatre on Xiafei Road and Hualong Road, is a masterpiece by the world-renowned "Fugitive" protagonist Paul Muni, breaking all previous amazing achievements. Therefore, Hualong Road will be congested at that time. Those who want to see a good film should come early to avoid missing it.
